<div id="review_2575054837" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2575054837" />
    <a title="Missy J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7406091-missy-j"><img alt="Missy J" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481102743p2/7406091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2575054837?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Missy J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Missy J" href="/user/show/7406091-missy-j">Missy J</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=africa-related">africa-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2575054837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13283360777463484052">4.5*<br/><br/>I have wanted to read this classic for a very long time, but was always hesitant to pick it up. What if I don't get it, the way I didn't enjoy and understand Doctor Zhivago or Midnight Children? Palace Walk is also quite a big book, so I kept putting it off. Until I made it a priority to read it before 2018 ends.<br/><br/>Wow, how mistaken I was! This book is so readable, the characters are so vivid and the plot was easy to follow. I love family sagas that are juxtaposed to the development of a nation</span>
  <span id="freeText13283360777463484052" style="display:none">4.5*<br /><br />I have wanted to read this classic for a very long time, but was always hesitant to pick it up. What if I don't get it, the way I didn't enjoy and understand Doctor Zhivago or Midnight Children? Palace Walk is also quite a big book, so I kept putting it off. Until I made it a priority to read it before 2018 ends.<br /><br />Wow, how mistaken I was! This book is so readable, the characters are so vivid and the plot was easy to follow. I love family sagas that are juxtaposed to the development of a nation/country. They really make the best historical fictions I find.<br /><br />Palace Walk is the home of al-Sayyid Ahmad Abd al-Jawad. He lives there with his subservient wife Amina and 5 of his children; Yasin, Fahmy, Khadija, Aisha and Kamal. Yasin is actually the son of Ahmad's first wife, before he divorced her and married Amina, who is more submissive to his tyrannical ways. Amina and the kids live in fear and respect of Ahmad, who actually displays a double personality. In front of his family, he is stern and demanding, but to his friends, he shows an easy-going, bon vivant personality. To his family, he pretends to be religious, but with his friends, he doesn't hesitate to drink and engage in adulterous affairs.<br /><br />We witness Amina's quiet suffering and how she copes with it by being very religious. Yasin has inherited his father's indulgent ways. Fahmy is a law student with ideal views. Khadija is the sharp-tongued daughter, whose huge nose might pose a problem to find a marriage partner. Aisha is the lazy and beautiful blonde daughter everybody adores. Kamal is still a young boy, who inherited his father's singing voice unbeknownst to everybody. We follow the first four children's transition from youth to adulthood/marriage. <br /><br />The reason I'm taking off 0.5 stars, is because the demonstrations described in the second half of the book were a bit slow-going for me. I was more interested in the family drama. But I enjoyed learning indirectly about Egypt's early modern history. I find that as long as it doesn't take away too much space of the family's story, it will hold my interest. <br /><br />At first, I wasn't sure if I would read the sequel of Palace Walk, but the ending was so intense, that I really want to know what is going to happen next to this family.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13283360777463484052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1921679482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1921679482" />
    <a title="dely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4579103-dely"><img alt="dely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487794781p2/4579103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1921679482?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="dely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="dely" href="/user/show/4579103-dely">dely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4579103-dely?shelf=0-egypt">0-egypt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1921679482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15881864105007478004">The reader follows the everyday life of the Abd al-Jawad family, living in Cairo, from early 1900 under British protectorate to the revolution of 1919. There isn't only the interesting historical background, but what I found more fascinating were the habits and customs of everyday life in this Egyptian family.<br/>There is the despotic father, Al-Sayyid Ahmad Abd al-Jawad, who terrorized the other members of the family; nice, friendly and a perfect buddy outside the household, but an unbearable fathe</span>
  <span id="freeText15881864105007478004" style="display:none">The reader follows the everyday life of the Abd al-Jawad family, living in Cairo, from early 1900 under British protectorate to the revolution of 1919. There isn't only the interesting historical background, but what I found more fascinating were the habits and customs of everyday life in this Egyptian family.<br />There is the despotic father, Al-Sayyid Ahmad Abd al-Jawad, who terrorized the other members of the family; nice, friendly and a perfect buddy outside the household, but an unbearable father and husband. There's Amina, his sweet but totally submissive wife, and five children, everyone with a different personality.<br />I liked everything of this book and the author is really able to put the reader in the household of Al-Sayyid Ahmad, in the streets of Cairo, among the protesters of the revolution, and to feel the fears and joys of the members of this family thanks to very detailed descriptions and an easy and flowing prose. <br /><br />Will soon start the second book of the trilogy, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5495.Palace_of_Desire" title="Palace of Desire by Naguib Mahfouz" rel="nofollow noopener">Palace of Desire</a>.</span>

<div id="review_3230529955" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3230529955" />
    <a title="Asma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97354050-asma"><img alt="Asma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602413106p2/97354050.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3230529955?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Asma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Asma" href="/user/show/97354050-asma">Asma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780307947109" href="/book/show/11446013-palace-walk">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97354050-asma?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97354050-asma?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97354050-asma?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97354050-asma?shelf=memorable-characters">memorable-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97354050-asma?shelf=memorable-ending-lines">memorable-ending-lines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97354050-asma?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97354050-asma?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3230529955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6024474658557095690"> "Palace Walk" is the first book in the famous Cairo trilogy. It is both a classic and historical fiction. <br/>It's packed with humour, wit and subtlety. Wonderful, diverse and colourful characters. All of them are very believable and have a place of their own. Mahfouz gives attention to each character as deserved. <br/><br/>Our man of the match, Al Sayyid Ahmad Abd al Jawad, is one of the most memorable characters in literature. Forget three-dimensions, he is a poly-dimensional character. His hypocrisy, doub</span>
  <span id="freeText6024474658557095690" style="display:none"> "Palace Walk" is the first book in the famous Cairo trilogy. It is both a classic and historical fiction. <br />It's packed with humour, wit and subtlety. Wonderful, diverse and colourful characters. All of them are very believable and have a place of their own. Mahfouz gives attention to each character as deserved. <br /><br />Our man of the match, Al Sayyid Ahmad Abd al Jawad, is one of the most memorable characters in literature. Forget three-dimensions, he is a poly-dimensional character. His hypocrisy, double standards and diplomatic skills are just matchless. He is a horrible, morally corrupt man. It's interesting to see how he and his eldest son Yasin contrive justifications for their sinful actions. <br /><br />Mahfouz creates an amazing atmosphere. I could imagine the house of Al Sayyid Ahmad , the streets, and these characters living their lives within the pages of this book.<br /> I particularly loved the setting of the novel in early twentieth century during WWI, the political and cultural dilemma and nationalist revolution.<br />Last one third of the book is mainly about political unrest, revolution and British occupation in Egypt.<br /><br />Lots of interesting themes in this book, and I found them relatable. You can find people like sharp-tounged Khadija and political enthusiast Fahmy in Pakistani houses, too. <br /><br />Mahfouz caught me off-guard with the ending; I was under the impression that clouds of chaos have passed and "all is well" <i> now</i>.<br /><br />The last lines complemented with the situation were heart-breaking!<br /><br /><i>"Visit me once each year,<br />For it's wrong to abandon people forever."</i><br /><br /><br />However, I didn't find anything special in writing. Don't know how would it read like in Arabic but I think the translation could've been a bit better.<br /><br />Recommend this book to everyone, it's very entertaining and has something for almost every kind of reader.<br /><br />P.S Don't get intimidated with the list of characters, they are introduced gradually and it's quite easy to keep track of them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6024474658557095690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21835906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9020934179447320522">I was frustrated with this book...I was expecting more...<br/>I struggled through the first 150 pages, just trying to become interested in the characters and see where the story was headed. The family was so far outside of my experience that I found them difficult to relate to. <br/><br/>The father was overbearing, cruel, distant, prideful and hypocritical. He saved his best and most pleasant traits for his friends and his family was left with a far-removed disciplinarian. And he never changed. Amina, the moth</span>
  <span id="freeText9020934179447320522" style="display:none">I was frustrated with this book...I was expecting more...<br />I struggled through the first 150 pages, just trying to become interested in the characters and see where the story was headed. The family was so far outside of my experience that I found them difficult to relate to. <br /><br />The father was overbearing, cruel, distant, prideful and hypocritical. He saved his best and most pleasant traits for his friends and his family was left with a far-removed disciplinarian. And he never changed. Amina, the mother, was subservient to her husband in every way, she never left her home, she lived in a constant state of fear for the jinn (ghosts) who inhabited the house, and she was content with her life because it was what God willed for her. And she never changed. The two daughters Aisha &amp; Khadija lived and breathed vibrantly in the first part of the book, and then after their marriages they disappeared, from the family circle and the plot, it was like they fell off the earth. And they never changed....<br /><br />I kept waiting for something to develop, for someone to change, to break out of the cirlce, to stand up to their father or just to do something!!! The book was written as part of the Cairo Trilogy, but I don't know if I even want to pick up the next in the series. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3189556036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3418074811079449420">The Palace Walk is a fascinating portrayal of domestic and political life in Cairo circa World War I. It reminds me of a Middle Eastern version of Little Women or My Brilliant Friend in that it presents a bygone era that is shockingly different from modern sensibilities. The drama of innocent transgressions and socially acceptable abuse is spellbinding.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3259909046" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3259909046" />
    <a title="Lauren " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1291915-lauren"><img alt="Lauren " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604235645p2/1291915.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3259909046?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren " href="/user/show/1291915-lauren">Lauren </a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=nobel-prize">nobel-prize</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=middle-east">middle-east</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=rtw21">rtw21</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=translated-works">translated-works</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=arab-arabic-lit">arab-arabic-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3259909046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14997645288806335602">PALACE WALK by Naguib Mahfouz, tr. from Arabic (Egypt) by William Maynard Hutchins and Olive E. Kenny / 1956 Arabic, 1990 English.<br/><br/>Mahfouz's first book in his famed Cairo Trilogy impressed me in it's scope, even if it took a few pages for me to "warm up" fully to it. At 500 pages, the book spends several short chapters setting the scene and introducing the large Al-Jawad family. Once that was set in my mind, I was easily drawn into this story.<br/><br/>Palace Walk follows al-Sayyid Ahmad and his wife Amina</span>
  <span id="freeText14997645288806335602" style="display:none">PALACE WALK by Naguib Mahfouz, tr. from Arabic (Egypt) by William Maynard Hutchins and Olive E. Kenny / 1956 Arabic, 1990 English.<br /><br />Mahfouz's first book in his famed Cairo Trilogy impressed me in it's scope, even if it took a few pages for me to "warm up" fully to it. At 500 pages, the book spends several short chapters setting the scene and introducing the large Al-Jawad family. Once that was set in my mind, I was easily drawn into this story.<br /><br />Palace Walk follows al-Sayyid Ahmad and his wife Amina, and their 5 children - 2 daughters and 3 sons through several years of the British Protectorate in Egypt (early 20th century). Al-Sayyid Ahmad is a tyrannical hypocritical patriarch, lording over his wife and children within the four walls of their home on Palace Walk in downtown Cairo. Yet, outside of these walls, he is a shopkeeper with a penchant for alcohol and parties, despite his facade of being a devout and traditional Muslim. This disconnect of who he is, and who he wants everyone to think he is forms the tension at the heart of the novel - affecting all members of his family for years to come.<br /><br />Large portions or this book read like a soap opera - funny antics, affairs, arranged marriages, but also heavy with harrowing events and abuse. It reads pretty swiftly with short chapters and lots of dialogue.<br /><br />Mahfouz spends a lot of time with his characters. The shades and hues of each person - what drives them, their flaws, their passions. Palace Walk delves into this family and all the sadness, the inequity, but also finds the moments of tenderness and love between sisters, mothers/sons, brothers, etc.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14997645288806335602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_389671407" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/389671407" />
    <a title="Isabelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/231580-isabelle"><img alt="Isabelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245483674p2/231580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/389671407?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isabelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isabelle" href="/user/show/231580-isabelle">Isabelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer389671407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16432147739050744914">This is the first installment of Mahfouz's Cairo trilogy. This first novel serves as an introduction to the Al-Jawad family, centered around its tyrannical patriarch Mr Ahmad. He rules his family with an iron fist, but luckily his family obligations do not stand in the way of his libertine nightlife. As daily life unfolds in Palace Walk, with its retinue of weddings, births, deaths, divorces, so does History in this Cairo of 1919, where the British rule starts to fray at the seams.<br/><br/>I was absolute</span>
  <span id="freeText16432147739050744914" style="display:none">This is the first installment of Mahfouz's Cairo trilogy. This first novel serves as an introduction to the Al-Jawad family, centered around its tyrannical patriarch Mr Ahmad. He rules his family with an iron fist, but luckily his family obligations do not stand in the way of his libertine nightlife. As daily life unfolds in Palace Walk, with its retinue of weddings, births, deaths, divorces, so does History in this Cairo of 1919, where the British rule starts to fray at the seams.<br /><br />I was absolutely fascinated by the subtle brilliance of Mahfouz's writing, most particularly by the way he built the whole novel around the idea of duality: Mr Ahmad by day and Mr Ahmad by night, the outside world and the closed world of the house, the house itself and the harem within it, the world of men and that of women, family and friends, power and obedience, the life of the body and that of the soul, and of course the most ominous duality of all: the English and the Egyptians.<br /> <br />This is a fantastic novel masterminded by a fantastic novelist... and a particularly good read now that Egypt has awakened...</span>
  <a data-text-id="16432147739050744914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12523899076294694753">I recall being completely consumed by this wonderful book, despite its tragic nature. The writing style propelled me forward as a reader, and the vivid depictions of the protagonists kept me involved cover to cover. It was only fifteen years later that I visited Cairo on my unique visit to Egypt in the 2000s, and I felt that it had truly not changed all that much, mopeds replacing the horsecarts, from Mahfouz's description. This is one that I need to go back and read again. It is also the best b</span>
  <span id="freeText12523899076294694753" style="display:none">I recall being completely consumed by this wonderful book, despite its tragic nature. The writing style propelled me forward as a reader, and the vivid depictions of the protagonists kept me involved cover to cover. It was only fifteen years later that I visited Cairo on my unique visit to Egypt in the 2000s, and I felt that it had truly not changed all that much, mopeds replacing the horsecarts, from Mahfouz's description. This is one that I need to go back and read again. It is also the best book in the trilogy.</span>

<div id="review_1460589951" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1460589951" />
    <a title="Dioni (Bookie Mee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/238527-dioni-bookie-mee"><img alt="Dioni (Bookie Mee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349352533p2/238527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1460589951?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dioni (Bookie Mee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dioni (Bookie Mee)" href="/user/show/238527-dioni-bookie-mee">Dioni (Bookie Mee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/5489.Palace_Walk">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/238527-dioni-bookie-mee?shelf=african-festival">african-festival</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/238527-dioni-bookie-mee?shelf=nobel">nobel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1460589951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2089721472108275149">Mee's rating: 4.5/5<br/><br/>First published at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.meexia.com/bookie/2016/05/palace-walk-naguib-mahfouz/'>http://www.meexia.com/bookie/2016/05/...</a><br/><br/>Palace Walk is the first novel in the Cairo Trilogy by the winner of 1988 Nobel Prize for Literature, from Egypt - Naguib Mahfouz. First published in 1956, the novel started in 1917 in the midst of WWI. Egypt was occupied by the British, and after the war was over, talks of independence were rampant.<br/><br/>We see Egypt through the viewpoint of a single family: the patriarch Ahmad Abd al-Jawad, his submissive wife Amina, and </span>
  <span id="freeText2089721472108275149" style="display:none">Mee's rating: 4.5/5<br /><br />First published at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.meexia.com/bookie/2016/05/palace-walk-naguib-mahfouz/">http://www.meexia.com/bookie/2016/05/...</a><br /><br />Palace Walk is the first novel in the Cairo Trilogy by the winner of 1988 Nobel Prize for Literature, from Egypt - Naguib Mahfouz. First published in 1956, the novel started in 1917 in the midst of WWI. Egypt was occupied by the British, and after the war was over, talks of independence were rampant.<br /><br />We see Egypt through the viewpoint of a single family: the patriarch Ahmad Abd al-Jawad, his submissive wife Amina, and their five children: 3 boys and 2 girls. Yasin is the oldest son of Ahmad from his first, divorced wife, while the other 4 children are Ahmad and Amina's. Fahmy the second son, is a studious and thoughtful high school student. The two daughters are Khadija and Aisha. The older Khadija is plump and sharp-tongue as a defense to her lack of beauty and jealousy of Aisha who is the more beautiful of the two, and therefore more marriageable. The youngest of them all is Kamal, around 10 years old, and is often the only character who is free to roam around, bridging the men and the women.<br /><br />The book is nearly 500 pages, but it didn't feel like one. It was a nice surprise to find that it was very readable. I read it in just a little over 2 weeks. The prose is quite verbose, so the book could be shorter, but the translation probably just follows the original quite closely. Lots of the sentences that the characters say for example are probably not long when said in Arabic, but becoming very verbose when translated into English.<br /><br />I like how we follow a rather ordinary Egyptian family. Yes Ahmad is a hypocrite and quite oppressive towards his family, and in turn Amina's obedience and passivity is hard to take for modern eyes. But I felt the drama isn't sensationalized. There's no domestic violence, no rape and no polygamy, which seem like ripe topics for books set in Middle Eastern or Islamic culture. I like that the oppression shown is more subtle. I would actually believe that this is what average family in Egypt at the turn of 20th century was like. Some variations of it is shown by the neighbors and friends of the family, for example Amina isn't allowed to go out at all by her husband, while the neighbor's wife is free to go out shopping by herself.<br /><br />Ahmad Abd al-Jawad is probably the character that readers would have most problem with. While he demands all his family members to be straight, obedient, and all around good Muslims, and has the same strict and faithful front himself, unbeknownst to his family he spends every night drinking, partying, and visiting women of pleasures. Despicable in a glance, and there is no excuse for it, but I feel like the double life he's living isn't so far away from our modern time. Who isn't familiar with the story of a straight looking person who has a big crack behind the facade?<br /><br />I think it's a bit unfair to simply judge the flaws of the culture because it doesn't conform to our modern sensibilities. Keep in mind that this is set a century ago, and to think that around the same time women in Britain over the age of 30 have just won the right to vote (1918).<br /><br />I think Palace Walk is exactly the kind of fiction that you'd read to learn about another culture and another way of thinking. I found the banter between the characters to be one of the most interesting aspects. Possibly the flirting in particular. You probably wonder how a society that is so divided between male and female, so rigid in the meaning of honor and shame, would mingle at all. Mahfouz exposes this skilfully in the verbal and non-verbal interactions between the characters. There's meaning in every word and gesture - slightly different perhaps with our time and culture - but the same concept for the same game.<br /><br />Based on this reading, I do plan to read the second and the third book in the trilogy. My GR book club is reading all three books together, but I don't like reading multiple books by the same author successively, so I will schedule the second book to read next year. This is the first work by Naguib Mahfouz that I read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2089721472108275149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GtpylpuzVVhXnsy4AYzDtqbCegqa89IqXhPwFmpWNQPO9CPnspHQSrHCDTiYoBZAgQMmeqs1r835r/pTKEbmSg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uA1yKZDZ9H7r2Nc8fUfPQtHTGGXFlBE3Kskp9lZxSTlsIyNYuftxbA2EFrzkaxq09hJEFfRSbNCNdSOzFGGacA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer11406337646185457162">Naguib Mahfouz (Arabic author profile: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273240._' rel='nofollow noopener'>نجيب محفوظ</a>) was an Egyptian writer who won the 1988 Nobel Prize for Literature. He published over 50 novels, over 350 short stories, dozens of movie scripts, and five plays over a 70-year career. Many of his works have been made into Egyptian and foreign films.</span>
  <span id="freeText11406337646185457162" style="display:none">Naguib Mahfouz (Arabic author profile: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273240._" rel="nofollow noopener">نجيب محفوظ</a>) was an Egyptian writer who won the 1988 Nobel Prize for Literature. He published over 50 novels, over 350 short stories, dozens of movie scripts, and five plays over a 70-year career. Many of his works have been made into Egyptian and foreign films.</span>
